His other mistresses included <a href="/wiki/Moll_Davis" title="Moll Davis">Moll Davis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nell_Gwyn" title="Nell Gwyn">Nell Gwyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Killigrew,_Viscountess_Shannon" title="Elizabeth Killigrew, Viscountess Shannon">Elizabeth Killigrew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Pegge" title="Catherine Pegge">Catherine Pegge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Walter" title="Lucy Walter">Lucy Walter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louise_de_K%C3%A9rouaille,_Duchess_of_Portsmouth" title="Louise de K\xc3\xa9rouaille, Duchess of Portsmouth">Louise de K\xc3\xa9rouaille, Duchess of Portsmouth</a>. As a result, in his lifetime he was often nicknamed "<a href="/wiki/Old_Rowley" title="Old Rowley">Old Rowley</a>", the name of his favourite racehorse, notable as a stallion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPearson1960147_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPearson1960147-85">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>His subjects resented paying taxes that were spent on his mistresses and their children,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutton1989338_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutton1989338-86">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> many of whom received dukedoms or earldoms. The present <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Buccleuch" title="Duke of Buccleuch">Dukes of Buccleuch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Richmond" title="Duke of Richmond">Richmond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Grafton" title="Duke of Grafton">Grafton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_St_Albans" title="Duke of St Albans">St Albans</a> descend from Charles in unbroken male line.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser1979413_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser1979413-87">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a>, was descended from two of Charles\'s illegitimate sons: the <a href="/wiki/Henry_FitzRoy,_1st_Duke_of_Grafton" title="Henry FitzRoy, 1st Duke of Grafton">Dukes of Grafton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lennox,_1st_Duke_of_Richmond" title="Charles Lennox, 1st Duke of Richmond">Richmond</a>. Diana\'s son, <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Prince William, Duke of Cambridge</a>, second in line to the British throne, is likely to be the first British monarch descended from Charles II.\n</p><p>Charles\'s eldest son, the <a href="/wiki/James_Scott,_1st_Duke_of_Monmouth" title="James Scott, 1st Duke of Monmouth">Duke of Monmouth</a>, led a rebellion against James II, but was defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sedgemoor" title="Battle of Sedgemoor">Battle of Sedgemoor</a> on 6 July 1685, captured and executed. James was eventually dethroned in 1688, in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a>. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhc-charles2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Gilt statue" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rhc-charles2.jpg/170px-Rhc-charles2.jpg" width="170" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rhc-charles2.jpg/255px-Rhc-charles2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rhc-charles2.jpg/340px-Rhc-charles2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="831" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhc-charles2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statue of Charles II (c. 1682) in ancient Roman dress by <a href="/wiki/Grinling_Gibbons" title="Grinling Gibbons">Grinling Gibbons</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hospital_Chelsea" title="Royal Hospital Chelsea">Royal Hospital Chelsea</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Looking back on Charles\'s reign, Tories tended to view it as a time of benevolent monarchy whereas Whigs perceived it as a terrible <a href="/wiki/Despotism" title="Despotism">despotism</a>. Today it is possible to assess him without the taint of partisanship, and he is seen as more of a lovable rogue\xe2\x80\x94in the words of his contemporary <a href="/wiki/John_Evelyn" title="John Evelyn">John Evelyn</a>, "a prince of many virtues and many great imperfections, debonair, easy of access, not bloody or cruel".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller1991382\xe2\x80\x93383_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller1991382\xe2\x80\x93383-88">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Wilmot,_2nd_Earl_of_Rochester" title="John Wilmot, 2nd Earl of Rochester">John Wilmot, 2nd Earl of Rochester</a>, wrote more lewdly of Charles:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><div class="poem">\n<p>Restless he rolls from whore to whore<br />\nA merry monarch, scandalous and poor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller199195_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller199195-89">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Charles, a patron of the arts and sciences, founded the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Observatory,_Greenwich" title="Royal Observatory, Greenwich">Royal Observatory</a> and supported the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a>, a scientific group whose early members included <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hooke" title="Robert Hooke">Robert Hooke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Boyle" title="Robert Boyle">Robert Boyle</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>. He was the personal patron of Sir <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">Christopher Wren</a>, the architect who helped rebuild London after the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_London" title="Great Fire of London">Great Fire</a> and who constructed the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hospital_Chelsea" title="Royal Hospital Chelsea">Royal Hospital Chelsea</a>, which Charles founded as a home for retired soldiers in 1682. As a patron of education, he founded a number of schools, including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Mathematical_School" title="Royal Mathematical School">Royal Mathematical School</a> in London and <a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_Hospital" title="The King&#39;s Hospital">The King\'s Hospital</a> in Dublin, as well as the Erasmus Smith schools in various parts of Ireland.\n</p><p>The anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/English_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="English Restoration">Restoration</a> (which was also Charles\'s birthday)\xe2\x80\x9429 May\xe2\x80\x94was recognised in England until the mid-nineteenth century as <a href="/wiki/Oak_Apple_Day" title="Oak Apple Day">Oak Apple Day</a>, after the Royal Oak in which Charles hid during his escape from the forces of Oliver Cromwell. Traditional celebrations involved the wearing of oak leaves but these have now died out.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser1979118_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser1979118-90">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Charles II is commemorated by statues in London\'s <a href="/wiki/Soho_Square" title="Soho Square">Soho Square</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheppard196651\xe2\x80\x9353_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheppard196651\xe2\x80\x9353-91">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> in Edinburgh\'s Parliament Square, in St Mary\'s Square in <a href="/wiki/Gloucester" title="Gloucester">Gloucester</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGloucester_City_Council_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGloucester_City_Council-92">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and near the south portal of <a href="/wiki/Lichfield_Cathedral" title="Lichfield Cathedral">Lichfield Cathedral</a>, and is <a href="/wiki/Cultural_depictions_of_Charles_II_of_England" title="Cultural depictions of Charles II of England">depicted extensively in literature and other media</a>. <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston, South Carolina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Kingstown,_Rhode_Island" title="South Kingstown, Rhode Island">South Kingstown, Rhode Island</a>, are named after him.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Titles.2C_styles.2C_honours_and_arms"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles,_styles,_honours_and_arms">Titles, styles, honours and arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_II_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Titles, styles, honours and arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_and_styles">Titles and styles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_II_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Titles and styles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>29 May 1630 \xe2\x80\x93 May 1638</b>: The Duke of Cornwall</li>\n<li><b>May 1638 \xe2\x80\x93 30 January 1649</b>: The Prince of Wales</li>\n<li><b>30 January 1649 \xe2\x80\x93 6 February 1685</b>: <i>His Majesty</i> The King</li></ul>\n<p>The official <a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">style</a> of Charles II was "Charles the Second, by the Grace of God, <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="List of monarchs of England">King of England</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Monarchs_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Monarchs of Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_Kings_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="English Kings of France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fidei_defensor" class="mw-redirect" title="Fidei defensor">Defender of the Faith</a>, etc."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/English_claims_to_the_French_throne" title="English claims to the French throne">claim to France</a> was only nominal, and had been asserted by every English monarch since <a href="/wiki/Edward_III_of_England" title="Edward III of England">Edward III</a>, regardless of the amount of French territory actually controlled.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_II_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>KG</b>: <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter" title="Order of the Garter">Knight of the Garter</a>, <i>21 May 1638</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir1996255\xe2\x80\x93257_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir1996255\xe2\x80\x93257-5">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms">Arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_II_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As Prince of Wales, Charles\'s coat of arms was the <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">royal arms</a> (which he later inherited), differenced by a <a href="/wiki/Label_(heraldry)" title="Label (heraldry)">label</a> of three points <a href="/wiki/Argent" title="Argent">Argent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAshmole1715534_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAshmole1715534-94">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> His arms as monarch were: <a href="/wiki/Quartering_(heraldry)" title="Quartering (heraldry)">Quarterly</a>, I and IV Grandquarterly, <a href="/wiki/Azure_(heraldry)" title="Azure (heraldry)">Azure</a> three <a href="/wiki/Fleurs-de-lis" class="mw-redirect" title="Fleurs-de-lis">fleurs-de-lis</a> <a href="/wiki/Or_(heraldry)" title="Or (heraldry)">Or</a> (for France) and <a href="/wiki/Gules" title="Gules">Gules</a> three lions <a href="/wiki/Attitude_(heraldry)#Passant" title="Attitude (heraldry)">passant guardant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pale_(heraldry)" title="Pale (heraldry)">pale</a> Or (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Arms_of_England" title="Royal Arms of England">for England</a>); II Or a lion <a href="/wiki/Rampant" class="mw-redirect" title="Rampant">rampant</a> within a double <a href="/wiki/Tressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Tressure">tressure</a> flory-counter-flory Gules (<a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal coat of arms of Scotland">for Scotland</a>); III Azure a harp Or stringed Argent (<a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Ireland" title="Coat of arms of Ireland">for Ireland</a>).\n</p>\n<table border="0" align="center" width="70%">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="33%"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Stuart_Princes_of_Wales_(1610-1688).svg" class="image"><img alt="Coat of Charles II as king (outside Scotland)</div>\n</td>\n<td><div style="text-align: center;">Coat of arms of Charles II used as king in Scotland</div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Issue">Issue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_II_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Issue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Descendants_of_Charles_II_of_England" title="Descendants of Charles II of England">Descendants of Charles II of England</a></div>\n<p>By <b><a href="/wiki/Lucy_Walter" title="Lucy Walter">Lucy Walter</a></b> (c. 1630 \xe2\x80\x93 1658)\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/James_Scott,_1st_Duke_of_Monmouth" title="James Scott, 1st Duke of Monmouth">James Crofts, later Scott</a> (1649\xe2\x80\x931685), created <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Monmouth" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Monmouth">Duke of Monmouth</a> (1663) in England and <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Buccleuch" title="Duke of Buccleuch">Duke of Buccleuch</a> (1663) in Scotland. Monmouth was born nine months after Walter and Charles II first met, and was acknowledged as his son by Charles II, but James II suggested that he was the son of another of her lovers, Colonel Robert Sidney, rather than Charles. Lucy Walter had a daughter, Mary Crofts, born after James in 1651, but Charles II was not the father, since he and Walter parted in September 1649.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeir1996255\xe2\x80\x93257_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeir1996255\xe2\x80\x93257-5">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>\n<p>By <b><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Killigrew,_Viscountess_Shannon" title="Elizabeth Killigrew, Viscountess Shannon">Elizabeth Killigrew</a></b> (1622\xe2\x80\x931680), daughter of Sir <a href="/wiki/Robert_Killigrew" title="Robert Killigrew">Robert Killigrew</a>, married <a href="/wiki/Francis_Boyle,_1st_Viscount_Shannon" title="Francis Boyle, 1st Viscount Shannon">Francis Boyle, 1st Viscount Shannon</a>, in 1660\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Charlotte_FitzRoy,_Countess_of_Yarmouth" title="Charlotte FitzRoy, Countess of Yarmouth">Charlotte Jemima Henrietta Maria FitzRoy</a> (1650\xe2\x80\x931684), married firstly James Howard and secondly <a href="/wiki/William_Paston,_2nd_Earl_of_Yarmouth" title="William Paston, 2nd Earl of Yarmouth">William Paston, 2nd Earl of Yarmouth</a></li></ol>\n<p>By <b><a href="/wiki/Catherine_Pegge" title="Catherine Pegge">Catherine Pegge</a></b>\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Charles_FitzCharles,_1st_Earl_of_Plymouth" title="Charles FitzCharles, 1st Earl of Plymouth">Charles FitzCharles</a> (1657\xe2\x80\x931680), known as "Don Carlo", created <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Plymouth" title="Earl of Plymouth">Earl of Plymouth</a> (1675)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Catherine_FitzCharles" title="Catherine FitzCharles">Catherine FitzCharles</a> (born 1658; she either died young or became a nun at Dunkirk)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutton1989125_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutton1989125-95">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>\n<p>By <b><a href="/wiki/Barbara_Palmer,_1st_Duchess_of_Cleveland" title="Barbara Palmer, 1st Duchess of Cleveland">Barbara n\xc3\xa9e Villiers</a></b> (1641\xe2\x80\x931709), wife of <a href="/wiki/Roger_Palmer,_1st_Earl_of_Castlemaine" title="Roger Palmer, 1st Earl of Castlemaine">Roger Palmer, 1st Earl of Castlemaine</a>; created <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Cleveland" title="Duke of Cleveland">Duchess of Cleveland</a> in her own right\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Anne_Lennard,_Countess_of_Sussex" title="Anne Lennard, Countess of Sussex">Lady Anne Palmer (Fitzroy)</a> (1661\xe2\x80\x931722), married <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lennard,_1st_Earl_of_Sussex" title="Thomas Lennard, 1st Earl of Sussex">Thomas Lennard, 1st Earl of Sussex</a>. She may have been the daughter of Roger Palmer, but Charles accepted her.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECokayne1926706\xe2\x80\x93708_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECokayne1926706\xe2\x80\x93708-96">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_FitzRoy,_2nd_Duke_of_Cleveland" title="Charles FitzRoy, 2nd Duke of Cleveland">Charles Fitzroy</a> (1662\xe2\x80\x931730), created <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Southampton" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Southampton">Duke of Southampton</a> (1675), became 2nd <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Cleveland" title="Duke of Cleveland">Duke of Cleveland</a> (1709)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_FitzRoy,_1st_Duke_of_Grafton" title="Henry FitzRoy, 1st Duke of Grafton">Henry Fitzroy</a> (1663\xe2\x80\x931690), created <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Euston" class="mw-redirect" title="Earl of Euston">Earl of Euston</a> (1672), <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Grafton" title="Duke of Grafton">Duke of Grafton</a> (1675)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Lee,_Countess_of_Lichfield" title="Charlotte Lee, Countess of Lichfield">Charlotte Fitzroy</a> (1664\xe2\x80\x931717), married <a href="/wiki/Edward_Lee,_1st_Earl_of_Lichfield" title="Edward Lee, 1st Earl of Lichfield">Edward Lee, 1st Earl of Lichfield</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_FitzRoy,_1st_Duke_of_Northumberland" title="George FitzRoy, 1st Duke of Northumberland">George Fitzroy</a> (1665\xe2\x80\x931716), created <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Northumberland" title="Earl of Northumberland">Earl of Northumberland</a> (1674), <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Northumberland" title="Duke of Northumberland">Duke of Northumberland</a> (1678)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lady_Barbara_FitzRoy" title="Lady Barbara FitzRoy">Barbara (Benedicta) Fitzroy</a> (1672\xe2\x80\x931737) \xe2\x80\x93 She was probably the child of <a href="/wiki/John_Churchill" class="mw-redirect" title="John Churchill">John Churchill</a>, later <a href="/wiki/Dukes_of_Marlborough" class="mw-redirect" title="Dukes of Marlborough">Duke of Marlborough</a>, who was another of Cleveland\'s many lovers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller199197,_123_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller199197,_123-97">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and was never acknowledged by Charles as his own daughter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser197965,_286_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser197965,_286-98">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>\n<p>By <b><a href="/wiki/Nell_Gwyn" title="Nell Gwyn">Nell Gwyn</a></b> (1650\xe2\x80\x931687)\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Beauclerk,_1st_Duke_of_St_Albans" title="Charles Beauclerk, 1st Duke of St Albans">Charles Beauclerk</a> (1670\xe2\x80\x931726), created <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_St_Albans" title="Duke of St Albans">Duke of St Albans</a> (1684)</li>\n<li>James, Lord Beauclerk (1671\xe2\x80\x931680)</li></ol>\n<p>By <b><a href="/wiki/Louise_de_K%C3%A9rouaille,_Duchess_of_Portsmouth" title="Louise de K\xc3\xa9rouaille, Duchess of Portsmouth">Louise Ren\xc3\xa9e de Penancoet de K\xc3\xa9rouaille</a></b> (1649\xe2\x80\x931734), created <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Portsmouth" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Portsmouth">Duchess of Portsmouth</a> in her own right (1673)\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Lennox,_1st_Duke_of_Richmond" title="Charles Lennox, 1st Duke of Richmond">Charles Lennox</a> (1672\xe2\x80\x931723), created <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Richmond" title="Duke of Richmond">Duke of Richmond</a> (1675) in England and <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Lennox" title="Duke of Lennox">Duke of Lennox</a> (1675) in Scotland.</li></ol>\n<p>By <b><a href="/wiki/Moll_Davis" title="Moll Davis">Mary \'Moll\' Davis</a></b>, courtesan and actress of repute<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser1979287_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser1979287-99">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Lady_Mary_Tudor" title="Lady Mary Tudor">Lady Mary Tudor</a> (1673\xe2\x80\x931726), married <a href="/wiki/Edward_Radclyffe,_2nd_Earl_of_Derwentwater" title="Edward Radclyffe, 2nd Earl of Derwentwater">Edward Radclyffe, 2nd Earl of Derwentwater</a>; after Edward\'s death, she married <a href="/wiki/Henry_Graham_(of_Levens)" title="Henry Graham (of Levens)">Henry Graham (of Levens)</a>, and upon his death she married James Rooke.</li></ol>\n<p>Other probable mistresses:\n</p>\n<ol><li>Christabella Wyndham<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hortense_Mancini" title="Hortense Mancini">Hortense Mancini</a>, Duchess of Mazarin<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Winifred_Wells" title="Winifred Roberts \xe2\x80\x93 the daughter of a clergyman<sup id="cite_ref-mrs_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrs-102">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Mrs Knight \xe2\x80\x93 a famous singer<sup Kildare</a><sup id="cite_ref-mrs_102-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrs-102">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>\n<p>Letters claiming that Marguerite or Margaret de Carteret bore Charles a son named <a href="/wiki/James_de_la_Cloche" title="James de la Cloche">James de la Cloche</a> in 1646 are dismissed by historians as forgeries.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_II_of_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-reign-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-reign_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The traditional date of the Restoration marking the first assembly of King and Parliament together since the abolition of the English monarchy in 1649. The English Parliament recognised Charles as king by unanimous vote on 2 May 1660, and he was proclaimed king in London on 8 May, although royalists had recognised him as such since the execution of his father on 30 January 1649. During Charles\'s reign all legal documents were dated as if his reign began at his father\'s death.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">From the death of his father to his defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Worcester" title="Battle of Worcester">Battle of Worcester</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">All dates in this article unless otherwise noted are given in the <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian calendar</a> with the start of year adjusted to 1 January (see <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">Old Style and New Style dates</a>).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One thousand pounds was a vast sum at the time, greater than an average workman\'s lifetime earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraser1979117_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraser1979117-16">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> </span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It cost the Treasury \xc2\xa3321,000 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHutton1989184_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHutton1989184-46">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> </span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The ship\'s transom is on display at the <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a> in Amsterdam.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span
